  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_e18ec293-163a-4748-85b8-730afdcb078a'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer18097495991747477330">Saman is a story filtered through the lives of its feisty female protagonists and the enigmatic “hero” Saman. It is at o­nce an exposé of the oppression of plantation workers in South Sumatra, a lyrical quest to understand the place of religion and spirituality in contemporary lives, a playful exploration of female sexuality and a story about love in all its guises, while </span>
  <span id="freeText18097495991747477330" style="display:none">Saman is a story filtered through the lives of its feisty female protagonists and the enigmatic “hero” Saman. It is at o­nce an exposé of the oppression of plantation workers in South Sumatra, a lyrical quest to understand the place of religion and spirituality in contemporary lives, a playful exploration of female sexuality and a story about love in all its guises, while touching o­n all of Indonesia’s taboos: extramarital sex, political repression and the relationship between Christians and Muslims.<br /><br />Saman has taken the Indonesian literary world by storm and sold over 100,000 copies in the Indonesian language, and is now available for the first time in English.<br /><br />ABOUT THE AUTHOR<br />Ayu Utami was born in Bogor, grew up in Jakarta and obtained her bachelor degree in Literature Studies from University of Indonesia. She worked as a journalist for Matra, Forum Keadilan, and D&amp;R. Not long after the New Order regime closed Tempo, Editor, and Detik, she participated in the founding of Indonesia’s Alliance of Independent Journalists to protest the closure of those three weeklys. Currently she is working for the cultural journal Kalam, and at Teater Utan Kayu. Saman was awarded the Prince Claus Award in the year 2000.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18097495991747477330" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

    <a title="John" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/285596-john"><img alt="John" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1268420679p2/285596.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8650710?book_show_action=true">Nov 04, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="John" class="user" itemprop="url" name="John" href="/user/show/285596-john">John</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/285596-john?shelf=indonesia">indonesia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8650710" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9850906509952844922">The story of an Indonesian activist told by a young female Javanese expat living in NYC and working for a human rights NGO. The writing is evocative, even sensual at times, and despite some rough edges it manages to paint a very convincing and fairly tragic picture of poor rural Indonesian communities being exploited and killed under the nose of a numb, corrupt state. <br/><br/>Against this setting, Saman, a former priest, stands up for a small community being violently pressured to sign over their lands </span>
  <span id="freeText9850906509952844922" style="display:none">The story of an Indonesian activist told by a young female Javanese expat living in NYC and working for a human rights NGO. The writing is evocative, even sensual at times, and despite some rough edges it manages to paint a very convincing and fairly tragic picture of poor rural Indonesian communities being exploited and killed under the nose of a numb, corrupt state. <br /><br />Against this setting, Saman, a former priest, stands up for a small community being violently pressured to sign over their lands to a new palm oil plantation. He is then captured, imprisioned and tortured, and manages to escpae. Saman's moral, political and philosophical digressions make for engaging reading, as does his sexual "awakening" later on. Sex, actually, playes a larger role in this novel than I would have suspected, putting in pretty stark relief the intense sexual repression in Indonesian society, particularly the smaller and more rural ones.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9850906509952844922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_111806434" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111806434" />
    <a title="Bronwyn Mauldin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4013102-bronwyn-mauldin"><img alt="Bronwyn Mauldin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1527282196p2/4013102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111806434?book_show_action=true">Jul 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bronwyn Mauldin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bronwyn Mauldin" href="/user/show/4013102-bronwyn-mauldin">Bronwyn Mauldin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4013102-bronwyn-mauldin?shelf=indie">indie</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111806434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1769407324458282298">Saman is the story of how a Catholic priest in the world’s most populous Muslim country, Indonesia, becomes a human rights activist called "Saman." Author, journalist Ayu Utami, turns the familiar tale of the crusader for justice on its head by folding Saman's story into that of a group of young women who knew him when they were school girls and he a newly-ordained priest.<br/><br/>Laila is the good girl who always falls for men she cannot have. Shakuntala the dancer who breaks her name in two for an Amer</span>
  <span id="freeText1769407324458282298" style="display:none">Saman is the story of how a Catholic priest in the world’s most populous Muslim country, Indonesia, becomes a human rights activist called "Saman." Author, journalist Ayu Utami, turns the familiar tale of the crusader for justice on its head by folding Saman's story into that of a group of young women who knew him when they were school girls and he a newly-ordained priest.<br /><br />Laila is the good girl who always falls for men she cannot have. Shakuntala the dancer who breaks her name in two for an American grant. Cok the bad girl exiled by her family. Yasmin the serious attorney trapped in a dull marriage. As these girls grow up and explore their sexual identities, the priest comes into his own, and with their help, is reborn.<br /><br />The story unfolds in layers, spanning the globe from one former Dutch colony (Indonesia) to another (New York), in only 180 pages. We read the story through several points of view, and through narrative, letters and emails. Watch for small details casually dropped along the way, as they add up to a powerful tale that is as much about the diversity of modern Indonesia as it is about any one person’s search for justice and freedom. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1769407324458282298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2867550057" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2867550057" />
    <a title="Missy J" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7406091-missy-j"><img alt="Missy J" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481102743p2/7406091.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2867550057?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Missy J" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Missy J" href="/user/show/7406091-missy-j">Missy J</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9799105706" href="/book/show/22779724-saman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=asia-related">asia-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=read-in-indonesian">read-in-indonesian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=2019-books">2019-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=indonesia-related">indonesia-related</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7406091-missy-j?shelf=southeast-asia">southeast-asia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2867550057" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14379119792417726152">Since I read an article about the author Ayu Utami a few years back, I have wanted to read one of her books for a long time already. She struck me as a very brave and forward-thinking female author in a country dominated by patriarchy. Earlier this year, I finally managed to buy a copy of Saman, even in its original language! Yay! Furthermore, it was the perfect length for me (just over 200 pages). <br/><br/>Well, what can I say now. I think I understand why this book mostly got average ratings. It starte</span>
  <span id="freeText14379119792417726152" style="display:none">Since I read an article about the author Ayu Utami a few years back, I have wanted to read one of her books for a long time already. She struck me as a very brave and forward-thinking female author in a country dominated by patriarchy. Earlier this year, I finally managed to buy a copy of Saman, even in its original language! Yay! Furthermore, it was the perfect length for me (just over 200 pages). <br /><br />Well, what can I say now. I think I understand why this book mostly got average ratings. It started off really good. We meet Laila, a photographer who is assigned to take promotional marketing photos for an oil drilling company. On site, she falls in love with Sihar Situmorang, a Batak engineer with a strong personality and penchant for justice. They witness a cruel accident and grow close to each other during the legal process. However, he is married and Laila much younger than him. During the legal process, we meet Saman and then suddenly the next 3/4 of the book focuses on him. We get a ghost story and we get another social justice issue - rubber farmers who are harassed by a palm oil company that wants to take away their land. Saman, who has taken his vows in a parish is completely obsessed by their troubles. Things get worse and Saman's path crosses again with the four women, whom the author supposedly focused on: Laila, Cok, Yasmin and Shakuntala. We never get a proper ending for Laila, which bothers me a lot. I wanted to know what happened to her and Sihar. Her story didn't fit at all with the second half of the book and Saman. I don't recall hearing Cok's voice. There are chapters narrated by Shakuntala, but I thought they were redundant. It was just her ranting about Laila's devotion to Sihar and how the friendship formed between the four women. Yasmin suddenly emerges towards the end of the book and took on an important role, but I didn't manage to warm up to her because the story was about something else before she even entered. So all in all, the story is all over the place. Maybe I should read the next book, so I can get some answers to my questions? Or will I just get more confused? What also annoyed me a lot are the many typos and errors in spelling. This book is like a mishmash of an Indonesian Sex in the City with a ghost story and several serious social justice issues (oil mining, palm oil company, freedom of press) thrown in.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14379119792417726152" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer7700539" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7909081718946085013">The first book by an indonesian writer I have ever read.<br/>I have to admit that I'm still a bit puzzled about the meaning and the symbols in it, but as I kept thinking about it and read more about the reactions this book provoced, I realized that it's a very brave book. Sexuality, religious conflicts, the effects the Transmigrasi policy in the 70s, friendship, love, everything is brought up here. It is both, the story of the main characters of the book and their moving fates and a reflection about </span>
  <span id="freeText7909081718946085013" style="display:none">The first book by an indonesian writer I have ever read.<br />I have to admit that I'm still a bit puzzled about the meaning and the symbols in it, but as I kept thinking about it and read more about the reactions this book provoced, I realized that it's a very brave book. Sexuality, religious conflicts, the effects the Transmigrasi policy in the 70s, friendship, love, everything is brought up here. It is both, the story of the main characters of the book and their moving fates and a reflection about Indonesia. I'll definately read it again later in my life because it still captivates me somehow, even though I can't exactly say why. One thing is for sure: It is an interesting story and the discussions this book unleashed make it worth reading.</span>

<div id="review_2753184395" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2753184395" />
    <a title="Desca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25616429-desca"><img alt="Desca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582311054p2/25616429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2753184395?book_show_action=true">Mar 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Desca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Desca" href="/user/show/25616429-desca">Desca</a>

<div id="review_2938207274" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2938207274?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rick Brose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rick Brose" href="/user/show/34210859-rick-brose">Rick Brose</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34210859-rick-brose?shelf=read-harder-2019-challenge">read-harder-2019-challenge</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2938207274" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14113993909122554941">Some translations can feel blocky and stagnant. The translation of Saman retains a flowing, poetic feel to it throughout the book. The novel is an intriguing narrative with complex characters and deep backgrounds. The Indonesian culture and history that is covered within the pages is captivating. It is not a book with a definitive beginning, middle, and end. That did not bother me though. I enjoyed digging into the lives, choices, and motivations of the characters presented.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2907300191" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2907300191" />
    <a title="Shelley Rose" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20375321-shelley-rose"><img alt="Shelley Rose" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1391560598p2/20375321.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2907300191?book_show_action=true">Jul 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelley Rose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelley Rose" href="/user/show/20375321-shelley-rose">Shelley Rose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2907300191" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4923349899964960310">3 stars for the first 100 pages; 1 star for most everything after that!<br/><br/>There are basically two different stories going on in this book. The first story is centered around Saman, a Catholic priest turned plantation worker rights activist. I really enjoyed his storyline and wish Utami had developed it even further. In this portion of the book, Utami highlights conditions in “transmigration” communities and the heavy hand of oil, rubber, and palm oil industries in Indonesia. We also see Saman explo</span>
  <span id="freeText4923349899964960310" style="display:none">3 stars for the first 100 pages; 1 star for most everything after that!<br /><br />There are basically two different stories going on in this book. The first story is centered around Saman, a Catholic priest turned plantation worker rights activist. I really enjoyed his storyline and wish Utami had developed it even further. In this portion of the book, Utami highlights conditions in “transmigration” communities and the heavy hand of oil, rubber, and palm oil industries in Indonesia. We also see Saman explore his sexuality and rethink his vow of celibacy. All good.<br /><br />Then, there is a secondary (and in my opinion, unnecessary) plot about four women who’ve been friends since their youth. This portion of the book basically serves as a chance to have female characters talk openly about their sexuality and voice their opinions on other societal issues. I didn’t find anything particularly intriguing about these women and the exploration of sexuality here really came off as...tasteless (?). While their story *sort of* ties into Saman’s, it didn’t do so cleanly.<br /><br />I was totally engaged in this book for the first 100 pages or so, and then it just lost me! It began to feel like Utami simply wanted to provide commentary on every taboo subject in Indonesia (to the detriment of meaningful plot development). Having said that, she certainly brings up important points about environmental and human exploitation, colonialism, orientalism, discrimination against Chinese in Indonesia, religion, and sexuality. I do recognize how important this book was when it was published in Indonesia in light of those taboos, but it really just didn’t work for me. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4923349899964960310" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2815257967" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5787834-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599757728p2/5787834.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2815257967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7003564740973335752">I read this book to fulfill the "#Own voices/Oceania" task for Read Harder. While I really enjoyed how in-depth the story of Saman and the plantation workers was, I was left feeling like I was missing something. We didn't get a wrap-up to most of the stories that I thought were central to the plot (anything having to do with Laila, Saman's mother's ordeal, etc.). It just ended up being a series of mostly unrelated snippets about repression that were never fleshed out.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3121334269" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3121334269" />
    <a title="Shrunkula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15161961-shrunkula"><img alt="Shrunkula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583581191p2/15161961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3121334269?book_show_action=true">Jan 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shrunkula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shrunkula" href="/user/show/15161961-shrunkula">Shrunkula</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3121334269" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16297746754849947235">Ayu Utami writings are splendid, this book is no exception. Sadly the plot, basically the romance part, did not grasps my interest. The book is written in three points of view, Laila, Shakuntala, and Saman yet somehow I found it a little bit disconnected from each other. Especially in the chapter where Shakuntala tells the story, mainly she talks about Laila's affair with a certain married man. It has little to no connection to Saman's part of the story. The book's title is Saman, obviously he's</span>
  <span id="freeText16297746754849947235" style="display:none">Ayu Utami writings are splendid, this book is no exception. Sadly the plot, basically the romance part, did not grasps my interest. The book is written in three points of view, Laila, Shakuntala, and Saman yet somehow I found it a little bit disconnected from each other. Especially in the chapter where Shakuntala tells the story, mainly she talks about Laila's affair with a certain married man. It has little to no connection to Saman's part of the story. The book's title is Saman, obviously he's the center of the overall plot, but he did not feel like the main character because Laila's love story takes a lot of portion of the book. <br /><br />I also find it al little bit elusive how Yasmin suddenly appears in the last chapter. We did not have her point of view and she's somehow a passive character because we only knows her form what others tells us. And in the last moment she somehow becomes one of the 'key characters' then the book is ending. I honestly dont know how to feel abot that. Also Cok, the supposed part of the pack, did not have a POV and very little connections to the overall plot (except for the part where she helps Saman. But that is it). <br /><br />I find Laila's story kinda boring in comparison to Shakuntala. She's the most interesting person in the whole book for me. She's an enigma and did not follow other's rule and her own story with her father and her point of view on everything is marvelous. And the fact that she's an overly honest, blunt, imaginative, and such a loving person to the one she truly cares about (cue Laila) makes her whole personality likeable. Also she makes some funny points on her narrative. <br /><br />A tiny bit about the sexual expression represented in this book, it released years before I was born, women have little to no saying about how they expressed their sexuality. And this book become a beacon. Each female that play part in this showed how fluid every form of sexual needs are and how women always shunned out from it. It is disgraceful if women shows even an ounce of sexual expression. And this book represented liberation and freedom of expressing. Even to this day it is still viewed disgraceful, but not as restricting as before. <br /><br />About Saman himself I find the part with his mother and her unborn children very appealing. And his personality changes makes the whole book bearable. I find that I can understands him a little. It is hard to stay as the person we used to be when we already witness and experience the injustice itself. Overall I think the point of 'lets wreck the system' in the whole book deserves a lot more spotlight than Laila's affair because honestly let's wreck the system. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16297746754849947235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3622234364" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3622234364" />
    <a title="Laura Faludi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5980689-laura-faludi"><img alt="Laura Faludi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542013923p2/5980689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3622234364?book_show_action=true">Oct 31, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura Faludi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura Faludi" href="/user/show/5980689-laura-faludi">Laura Faludi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3622234364" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11380238551567179319">I am not sure what to think. I really wanted to like this more. It is a jumble of some great ideas, sometimes clumsy writing and semi-developed characters. Part of if might have been the awkwardness of the translation (from Indonesian to English to Hungarian), partly the writer's indecisiveness on her priorities. Although the book's title is Saman, it was still marketed as a novel of sexual awakening of four Indonesian women, all of whom are connected to the mysterious Saman. Out of the four wom</span>
  <span id="freeText11380238551567179319" style="display:none">I am not sure what to think. I really wanted to like this more. It is a jumble of some great ideas, sometimes clumsy writing and semi-developed characters. Part of if might have been the awkwardness of the translation (from Indonesian to English to Hungarian), partly the writer's indecisiveness on her priorities. Although the book's title is Saman, it was still marketed as a novel of sexual awakening of four Indonesian women, all of whom are connected to the mysterious Saman. Out of the four women, we learn next to nothing about Cok, Leila's story is dropped halfway through (with minimal mentions of her early infatuation with Saman/Wis) and the only glimpse we have at Yasmin is through a section of short emails and her brief affairs with Saman. The only real POW is of Sakuntala's, but despite some interesting attempts to explore her relationship to her body through dancing, she quickly turns into an instrument of exposition and commentary on Leila's relationship. We do end up spending the most time, as the title suggests, with Saman, by far with the most compelling storyline of a priest turned activist battling his demons (literary and metaphoric), his doubt in the existence of a higher power and his own responsibilities towards the plantation workers. A plethora of important topics are touched upon (transmigrasi, landgrabbing, corruption, police violence, anti-Chinese sentiments, public health issues etc.) and dropped again (some of which could alone fill the book), leaving behind a sense of confusion and the question "now what?". I know that there is a sequel, but that does not explain why this book feels like a first draft/beginning of something, rather than the actual end product.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11380238551567179319" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2844598227" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2844598227" />
    <a title="Kat" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5868871-kat"><img alt="Kat" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2844598227?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat" href="/user/show/5868871-kat">Kat</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2844598227" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12078577403697970299">While travelling through Bali and Java I was excited to read the work of an Indonesian author. The variety of written structures is engaging, with different characters giving their perspectives at different times and through different mediums (ending in letters and emails). My main criticism is that the story felt rushed and characters were introduced with purpose only for their narratives to not be fully finished. The backdrop of the story is political unrest in Indonesia during the 1980's and </span>
  <span id="freeText12078577403697970299" style="display:none">While travelling through Bali and Java I was excited to read the work of an Indonesian author. The variety of written structures is engaging, with different characters giving their perspectives at different times and through different mediums (ending in letters and emails). My main criticism is that the story felt rushed and characters were introduced with purpose only for their narratives to not be fully finished. The backdrop of the story is political unrest in Indonesia during the 1980's and 1990's but while this content was interesting historically, the telling of it felt hollow and seemed only to provide a setting for the novel's more lascivious, primary goal of exploring modern Asian sexuality. This part of the story is done somewhat more artfully, starting with the naivety of a virgin, then continuing to the experimentation of teenagers and ending in the powerful sexual dominance of an adult woman who knows what she wants. However while this should be a story of female empowerment it ends as abruptly as male orgasm with no epilogue of any kind, which seemed like a missed opportunity to answer some of the questions the novel itself raises.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12078577403697970299" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5200859020826232947">I think maybe a lot of this just went over my head. I loved Saman as a character and I liked the others well enough. I recognized the thread that held them all together as a cast. I appreciate that the book pushed boundaries when published in Indonesia, touching on the cruelty and oppression in famers' lives, repressive sexual attitudes, religion, transmigration and politics, etc. But in the actual reading of it, I thought the whole thing felt disjointed. At one point (about halfway through) I a</span>
  <span id="freeText5200859020826232947" style="display:none">I think maybe a lot of this just went over my head. I loved Saman as a character and I liked the others well enough. I recognized the thread that held them all together as a cast. I appreciate that the book pushed boundaries when published in Indonesia, touching on the cruelty and oppression in famers' lives, repressive sexual attitudes, religion, transmigration and politics, etc. But in the actual reading of it, I thought the whole thing felt disjointed. At one point (about halfway through) I actually turned the book over to reread the synopsis to ensure it wasn't actually a series of interconnected short stories. And the little twist at the end (especially the last two emails) came so out of left field that I was left baffled. For all that, there is some beautiful writing here and Saman is a character you can't help but root for. </span>

    <a title="Seamus Gregan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/122450601-seamus-gregan"><img alt="Seamus Gregan" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3581117732" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer1429123586733257529">Well crafted, fully realised characters with shocking insight into the levels of exploitation in postcolonial societies. There are several parts, especially toward the beginning, that feel white-knuckle and almost as if the author is about to go supernova. It just...doesn't quite happen that way. Not that the latter half is weak, it's just not as satisfying as I'd hoped. But perhaps that's the point.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2821851328" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2821851328" />
    <a title="Lekeisha The Booknerd" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10666444-lekeisha-the-booknerd"><img alt="Lekeisha The Booknerd" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1450269973p2/10666444.jpg" /></a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PzmzcvfvIsrbV/kzsdK/H2MQdqAnIXntwXOD8EQezEK+U3Nah8Q6S/LU8FtG8dZjLpj6HAAonLwRVKztQtxBdg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gidtgtuysmeUpsl46B7SWuKfqlzAB5SBtKzJQ/KiHaUDTa2qq5mq5r0lwBAfPbsmrxcm4OcOcdBki+Ze9GCQkQ==')})
  }

Pada saat yang sama, Dimas menerima kabar dari Jakarta: Hananto Prawiro, sahabatnya, ditangkap tentara dan dinyatakan tewas. Dimas merasa cemas dan gamang. Bersama puluhan wartawan dan seniman lain, dia tak bisa kembali ke Jakarta karena paspornya dicabut oleh pemerintah Indonesia. Sejak itu mereka mengelana tanpa status yang jelas dari Santiago ke Havana, ke Peking dan akhirnya mendarat di tanah Eropa untuk mendapatkan suaka dan menetap di sana.\n\nDi tengah kesibukan mengelola Restoran Tanah Air di Paris bersama tiga kawannya: Nug, Tjai, dan Risjaf—mereka berempat disebut Empat Pilar Tanah Air—Dimas, terus-menerus dikejar rasa bersalah karena kawan-kawannya di Indonesia satu persatu tumbang, dikejar, ditembak, atau menghilang begitu saja dalam perburuan Peristiwa 30 September. Kesejatian hidup ada pada selembar daun kering yang gugur\ntertiup angin. Kesejatian hidup ada air susu ibu yang yang merelakan puting\npayudaranya diisap oleh bayi manapun. Di\nVihara Pit Yong Kiong, Pasuruan, di pelabuhan Belawan, di Penang, di\nBangkok, di Laos, di Golden Triangle, di Cambodia, di Bandung, di\nmanapun kau hidup.\n\nTapi, dia mungkin tak terlihat pada arus politik yang menyudutkanmu pada\npilihan kedigdayaan. Dia menyembunyikan diri dari teriakan-\nteriakan yang menggemakan perubahan. Kesejatian hidup tak memerlukan\nperubahan, namun juga tak menampiknya. Dia rebah pada semua kesederhanaan\nyang ada di sekelilingmu. Maka, carilah, dan kamu akan mendapatinya.\nKetuklah, maka pintu akan dibukakan bagimu. Mintalah, maka kau akan diberi.\n\nDemikianlah Dewi Lestari mewakilkan sebuah upaya pencarian kesejatian hidup\npada seorang tokoh bernama Bodhi. Seorang bayi yang di suatu pagi tergeletak\ndi pintu Vihara. Dipungut, diasuh, dan dididik oleh seorang Pandita, Guru\nLiong. Merasa bahwa karma pada hidup masa lalunya sangat berat. 18 tahun\ndididik dengan ketat, termasuk penguasaan terhadap sebuah ilmu bela diri,\nBodhi mengalami penyempurnaan bathin. Pemurnian spirit. Termasuk sejumlah\npengalaman uniknya yang &quot;merasa&quot; menjadi ulat, tikus got, kucing, dan sapi.\n\n18 tahun adalah waktu yang cukup, dan Bodhi mohon pamit. Bersama serombongan\npendeta Buddha, Bodhi menyeberang ke Sumatera dan memutuskan menetap di\ndaerah Belawan. Tanpa KTP, tak juga faham mengenai asal usul dan tanggal\nkelahirannya. Bekerja tiga bulan, mendapat upah, dan dibantu oleh Ompu\nBerlin untuk mendapatkan sejumlah dokumen identitas termasuk paspor, Bodhi\nmenyeberang ke Penang. Disana dia bertemu dengan sejumlah backpackers yang\nkemudian &quot;memberi&quot; arah perjalanan berikutnya: Bangkok.\n\nBangkok surga bagi para backpackers. Ratusan pengelana dari mancanegara\ntumpah di sana. Bodhi tinggal di semua rumah penginapan Srinthip bersama\nsejumlah backpakers multi etnis. Penghuninya datang dan pergi. Masuklah\nKell, seorang lelaki tampan, peranakan Irlandia dan Mesir. Lelaki tertampan\nyang mungkin pernah ada di bumi ini yang mempunyai tugas kehidupan untuk\nmembubuhkan 617 tatto pada 617 orang untuk membuat dirinya menyongsong\nkemerdekaan paripurna setelah orang ke-617 membubuhkan tato yang ke-618 ke\ntubuhnya. Lelaki yang kerap menyenandungkan Eye in The Sky-nya Alan Parson\nProject. Kell kemudian mengajarinya tattoo. Lalu, jadilah Bodhi seorang\ntattooist dan menjadikan itu sebagai cara untuk mendapatkan uang bagi biaya\nhidup sehari-hari.\n\nSeorang backpacker perempuan bernama Star, berasal dari Hollywood, peranakan\nEropa Timur dan Timur Tengah masuk dan menginap di Srinthip. Perempuan\ncantik dan tercantik yang pernah dilihat Bodhi. Perawakan tubuhnya sempurna.\nPerempuan inilah yang memperkenalkan dirinya dengan sebuah perasaan lain\nyang belum pernah dia rasakan sepanjang hidup. Star minta Bodhi mentattoonya\ntepat di payudara.Dan bergetarlah kulit semesta. Bergerolalah gelombang\nsamudera. Erangan kesakitan Star sewaktu ditattoo adalah hasrat dedaunan\nyang mendambakan sapuan sinar matahari. Waktu berlalu dan mereka berpisah.\nEntah kenapa.\n\nBodhi meneruskan pencarian kesejatiannya. Star seolah menggenap kesempurnaan\ntattoonya dan pergi menyongsong kelana berikut.\nKeterserakan yang tak menyenangkan. Tapi hidup adalah keping-keping misteri\nyang baru terbuka setelah rebah sepenuhnya. Bodhi membiarkan semesta\nmenuntun perjalanan selanjutnya. Bertemu kembali dengan Tristan, backpacker yang ditemuinya\npertama kali di Penang. Mereka berdua bekerja di ladang ganja di Golden\nTriangle dengan upah USD 700 per minggu. Sekian bulan di sana Bodhi memiliki\ncukup uang untuk melanjutkan kembara berikutnya. Pulang ke Srinthip\ndidapatinya Kell sudah tak ada. Ah, lelaki yang telah memberinya keceriaan\ndan sebuah warna baru.\n\nRasa kangennya memuncak. Diputuskannya untuk pergi mencari Kell. Tak ada\npetunjuk. Tak ada berita. Dan dia pergi. Suara semesta dan kerinduannya\nadalah dua buah kompas sejati yang dia percaya akan mengantarkannya tepat\nwaktu - tepat arah kepada Kell. Bodhi terdampar di sebuah pertarungan antar\nmanusia ala Golden Triangle ditonton oleh ribuan petaruh. Diadu secara\nbarbar di atas ring melawan gladiator raksasa. Pertarungan dahsyat dengan\nmenggunakan sejumlah jurus wushu yang mendebarkan pun digelar.\n\nPerjalanan itu begitu panjang dan melelahkan. Menembus belukar di antara\ndesingan peluru. Menyusuri daratan ranjau. Disana dia betemu Epona, gadis\npenakluk ranjau. Disana pula ia bertemu kembali dengan Kell. Lalu, pada\nsebuah kunjungan ke lokasi ranjau, tattoo ke 618, angka kebebasan paripurna\nKell, dirajahkan. Dalam dialog cerdas, konyol, menggelikan, dan bertabur air\nmata. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17914515061497289481">Justina Ayu Utami atau hanya Ayu Utami (lahir di Bogor, Jawa Barat, 21 November 1968) adalah aktivis jurnalis dan novelis Indonesia, ia besar di Jakarta dan menamatkan kuliah di Fakultas Sastra Universitas Indonesia.<br/>Ia pernah menjadi wartawan di majalah Humor, Matra, Forum Keadilan, dan D&R. Tak lama setelah penutupan Tempo, Editor dan Detik pada masa Orde Baru, ia ikut mendirikan Aliansi Jurnalis</span>
  <span id="freeText17914515061497289481" style="display:none">Justina Ayu Utami atau hanya Ayu Utami (lahir di Bogor, Jawa Barat, 21 November 1968) adalah aktivis jurnalis dan novelis Indonesia, ia besar di Jakarta dan menamatkan kuliah di Fakultas Sastra Universitas Indonesia.<br />Ia pernah menjadi wartawan di majalah Humor, Matra, Forum Keadilan, dan D&amp;R. Tak lama setelah penutupan Tempo, Editor dan Detik pada masa Orde Baru, ia ikut mendirikan Aliansi Jurnalis Independen yang memprotes pembredelan. Kini ia bekerja di jurnal kebudayaan Kalam dan di Teater Utan Kayu. Novelnya yang pertama, Saman, mendapatkan sambutan dari berbagai kritikus dan dianggap memberikan warna baru dalam sastra Indonesia.<br /><br />Ayu dikenal sebagai novelis sejak novelnya Saman memenangi sayembara penulisan roman Dewan Kesenian Jakarta 1998. Dalam waktu tiga tahun Saman terjual 55 ribu eksemplar. Berkat Saman pula, Ayu mendapat Prince Claus Award 2000 dari Prince Claus Fund, sebuah yayasan yang bermarkas di Den Haag, yang mempunyai misi mendukung dan memajukan kegiatan di bidang budaya dan pembangunan. Akhir 2001, ia meluncurkan novel Larung.</span>
